## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics
**Analysis**: This task models the acceleration (dv/dt) of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator, where the restoring force depends nonlinearly on position x, and damping/driving forces may depend on velocity v and time t. The equation of motion is dv/dt = F(x, v, t).

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Duffing with damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring + damping)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (driven cubic oscillator)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (1 - c2 * x**2) * v (nonlinear damping)
- Quintic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order restoring force)
- Quadratic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 (asymmetric restoring force)
- Nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * x**2 (position-dependent damping)
- Cubic damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (nonlinear velocity damping)
- Driven damped oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (sinusoidal driving force)
- Helmholtz oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * v (quadratic nonlinearity with damping)
- General polynomial restoring: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 + c3 * v (combined nonlinearities)
- Softening/hardening spring: dv_dt = c0 * x * (1 + c1 * x**2) (amplitude-dependent frequency)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope ŌåÆ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects ŌåÆ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay ŌåÆ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior ŌåÆ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects ŌåÆ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x**3, x**5) preserve oscillator symmetry; even powers (x**2) break symmetry and introduce asymmetric oscillations
- Position-dependent damping terms like (1 - c*x**2)*v indicate self-excited oscillations (limit cycles) as in Van der Pol systems
- Cubic position terms x**3 with same/opposite sign as linear term x indicate hardening/softening spring behavior (Duffing-type)
- Velocity terms proportional to v represent linear energy dissipation; v**3 or v*|v| represent nonlinear drag
- Periodic driving forces appear as sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) with no dependence on x or v, representing external forcing
- Cross terms like x*v indicate coupling between position and velocity that can produce complex phase-space trajectories
- Absence of explicit time dependence t suggests an autonomous system where energy is either conserved or dissipated monotonically
- Rational restoring forces like x/(1 + c*x**2) model bounded/saturating restoring forces for large displacements

Combining the x terms:
`-3.39285482994202*x - 3.39285482994202*x = -6.78570965988404*x`

So GT = `-3.39285482994202*x**3 - 6.78570965988404*x - 0.264872938986498*x*Abs(v)**(1/3) + 0.523287159969136*sin(t) - 0.710540944238196*Abs(v)**(1/3)`

The GT contains these structural elements:
1. `x**3` term
2. `x` term
3. `x * |v|^(1/3)` term (cross term between x and a fractional power of |v|)
4. `sin(t)` term
5. `|v|^(1/3)` term

Key observations:
- The GT involves `|v|^(1/3)`, which is a cube root of |v|. This is NOT equivalent to `v^2`, `log(v^2+1)`, `exp(v^2)`, or any standard function of v appearing in the candidates.
- The GT has a cross term `x * |v|^(1/3)` which couples x and v in a specific way.

Now let me check all candidates. Every candidate uses functions of v like: `v**2`, `exp(v**2)`, `log(v**2+1)`, `v**2*exp(...)`, `v**2*x**2`, etc. None of them contain `|v|^(1/3)` or any fractional power of |v|.

For a candidate to match, setting exponential/log terms to zero would eliminate the v-dependence entirely, but the GT has v-dependent terms (`|v|^(1/3)` and `x*|v|^(1/3)`). So we can't simply zero out v-dependent terms.

Could any v-dependent term in the candidates replicate `|v|^(1/3)`? 
- `v**2` ŌēĀ `|v|^(1/3)` for all v
- `log(c*v**2 + 1)` ŌēĀ `|v|^(1/3)` for all v (different behavior)
- `exp(c*v**2)` ŌēĀ `|v|^(1/3)` for all v
- No combination of these can produce `|v|^(1/3)` for all v

Additionally, the cross term `x*|v|^(1/3)` requires a product of x with a fractional power of v. Looking at candidates:
- Candidate 13 has `c8*x*log(c9*v**2 + 1)` - this is `x*log(...)` not `x*|v|^(1/3)`
- Candidate 36 has `c8*v**2*x` - this is `x*v**2` not `x*|v|^(1/3)`
- Candidate 25 has `c2*v**2*x**2` - wrong form

None of the candidates have any mechanism to produce `|v|^(1/3)` or the cross term `x*|v|^(1/3)`.

Since the GT fundamentally requires `|v|^(1/3)` terms (both standalone and multiplied by x), and no candidate formula can produce fractional powers of |v|, no candidate can match the GT.

Now I'll check each candidate. The critical issue is that none of the candidates contain `|v|^(1/3)` or `x*|v|^(1/3)`. Instead, they use `v┬▓`, `exp(v┬▓)`, `log(v┬▓+1)`, etc.

**Can any of these substitute for |v|^(1/3)?**

- `v┬▓` is an even function of v but has different growth behavior than `|v|^(1/3)` ŌĆö NOT equivalent
- `log(c*v┬▓+1)` ŌĆö this is even in v, but `log(c*v┬▓+1)` cannot equal `a*|v|^(1/3) + b` for all v
- `exp(c*v┬▓)` ŌĆö exponential, cannot match power law
- None of these basis functions can produce `|v|^(1/3)` or `x*|v|^(1/3)`

The GT requires `|v|^(1/3)` (a fractional power) and `x*|v|^(1/3)` (a cross term). No candidate contains these basis functions. By the linear independence principle, combinations of `v┬▓`, `log(v┬▓+1)`, `exp(v┬▓)`, etc., cannot exactly reproduce `|v|^(1/3)` for all values of v.

Let me verify each candidate systematically ŌĆö every single one uses combinations of `v┬▓`, `exp(v┬▓)`, `log(v┬▓+1)`, or similar, but **none** contain `|v|^(1/3)` or any fractional power of |v|. Similarly, none contain the cross term `x*|v|^(1/3)`.

Therefore, **no candidate can match the GT**.
